### Post by fedex1993 on 2009-01-31
February 2008 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

    * Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
    * If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
    * Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
    * The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
    * The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
    * Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
    * To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

      Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

      Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

      Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

      Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

      Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

Sorry i started the thread early again. Also needs to be stickied

---

### Post by phrostbyte on 2009-02-01
Pretty much last month. Also known as the lazy mans theme, because it took me about a minute to set up. 

Wallpaper: Killer Tux (google it)

Conky: Basically the default with fortune replaced with "fortune | cowsay" [get cowsay in one click.]("apt://cowsay") [and conky in another.]("apt://conky")

Theme: From [community-themes]("apt://community-themes") <-- all and all a good package to have installed! (Ubuntu 8.10 or higher)

Fonts: [Liberation font set]("apt://ttf-liberation")

Bash prompt: From the bash-prompts.sh in community script repo in my sig. No one click install for this (yet), sorry. :(

### Post by crimesaucer on 2009-02-01
> **TalioGladius said:**
> Very very nice.  I kind of want info on everything about it.

This is difficult to do since I customize everything myself:


- I use the murrine-svn engine and write my own gtkrc themes.
- I also make my own Emerald theme. This one uses the close buttons of a theme called "Radial")
- Icons are both the hydroxygene icon pack and the MacUltimate Leporard buttons. (I replace the gtk-buttons in the hydroxygene with the Apple ones for my browser/file manager)
- Some icons are from the iComity for my xfce4-panel launchers.
- The xfce4-panel is using a cairo patch for RGBA transparency.
- Font is called LucidaMACBold.
- Screenlets have all been modified to use different .png and .svg images and I also edit the python scripts to use my LucidaMACBold font and change the pager's colors.
- Slim theme is also the same as my wallpaper to seamlessly go from login to desktop.
- I also use a gtkrc-2.0 for my xfce4-panel for button/font colors.
- And the conkyrc is my own custom script that I made.


..... I might upload some of my murrine-svn gtk themes one of these days.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-02-02

The style should be available in the Themes and Styles Section at kde-look mate. The link that you have posted here, is a KDE screenshot link and it is obvious that its from the KDE Screenshot section and not themes and styles section. xfce-dark gtk
katiola windowborder

### Post by Piraja on 2009-02-03
> **sertse said:**
> Hey guys, where are you getting tint2 from? Looks good :)
[SIZE=6][FONT=Impact]_[[COLOR=Sienna]How to install Tint2 (an easy way)[/COLOR]]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6656314&postcount=4")_[/FONT][/SIZE]

Quoting [myself in another thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6656314&postcount=4"): 

> FYI, tint2 can be most easily installed on Intrepid via toodumbforgentoo's PPA repo:

deb [http://ppa.launchpad.net/k-belding/ppa/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/k-belding/ppa/ubuntu) intrepid main

Just add the line above to your /etc/apt/sources.list, perform "sudo apt-get update" and "sudo apt-get install tint2".**P.S.** That is the method and repository which I personally used, found after failing, for an unknown reason, to install by other means. [Killeroid]("https://launchpad.net/%7Ekilleroid/+archive/ppa") has a PPA repo from which you can install an unstable SVN version of Tint2, as I noticed through the link in his signature (see e.g. post [#140]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6673428&postcount=140") later in this thread). 

**NB!** _**[[COLOR=DarkOrange]Killeroid asked me to add this caveat:[/COLOR]]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6675073&postcount=153")**_
> 
After tint's last stable release(0.6), the developer renamed the binary to tint2 and changed the location and format of the tintrc files and also fixed some bugs(including the "window title does not update" bug) and added new features .
The new tint binary is found at /usr/bin/tint2 and the new tint conf file is found in ~/.config/tint2/ and the config file is now named tint2rc.
Since the format of the conf file has changed, old tintrc files wont work with the svn builds of tint.No worries though, tint still ships with a default tint2rc and some sample tint2rc files(found here /usr/share/doc/tint2/examples/ ) .
So anyone who uses the svn builds from my PPA, please take notice and also read the notice on the PPA page before you complain.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-02-04
> **CrazyDesi said:**
> Requesting wallpaper.   How do you get fluxboxs taskbar to go across the screen?  I have never been able to do that.

Sure thing!

[[img]http://omploader.org/tMTdrZQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMTdrZQ) 

You mean the toolbar. Right click on the toolbar and you will have an option called Toolbar Width Percent. Choose it and then right click continuously to increase the width! Otherwise you can always add this entry in your init file in .fluxbox directory. There must be an entry there already. But you can change the percentages according to your will.

```
session.screen0.toolbar.widthPercent: 100
```

hope that helps.

---

### Post by Killeroid on 2009-02-04
> **Piraja said:**
> Heyyy Killeroid, I just notice your sig and updated [my post #108]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6666969&postcount=108") accordingly. Very nice! (Especially the ram in the album cover... say no more!)

Heh, thanks. Glad to be of help. 
And if you could add a little notice in bold to everyone to read the notice  on the PPA page before adding the repo to the sources.list
or you can summarize what I just said below.

After tint's last stable release(0.6), the developer renamed the binary to tint2 and changed the location and format of the tintrc files and also fixed some bugs(including the "window title does not update" bug) and added new features .
 The new tint binary is found at /usr/bin/tint2  and the new tint conf file is found in ~/.config/tint2/ and the config file is now named tint2rc. 
Since the format of the conf file has changed, old tintrc files wont work with the svn builds of tint.No worries though, tint still ships with a default tint2rc and some sample tint2rc files(found here /usr/share/doc/tint2/examples/ ) .
So anyone who uses the svn builds from my PPA, please take notice and also read the notice on the PPA page before you complain.

---

### Post by Piraja on 2009-02-05
> **urukrama said:**
> What is the name of the terminal font you use?
Of the three [fonts in the screenshot*] you probably mean [My Underwood]("http://www.dafont.com/my-underwood.font"). More info available through the thumbnail link (or here: [my Ourdesktops page]("http://www.ourdesktops.com/desktop/user/A.%20F.%20K.%20A.%20Piraja")).

I just realized — or re-realized — I'm an idiot. The attached image gives a clue of what I mean.**
___

* I'm an idiot also because I read "terminal" and thought of "conky", however. The terminal font is indeed My Underwood, but in the three conky monitors you can see also LMTypewriter10 and ConkyWeather fonts. Sorry.

** What was that all about, eh? Well, I thought the strange spot that was printed in the terminal instead of the left arrow sign or whatever it's called ("<") either intentionally or unintentionally looked like an "ink stain", such as the old typewriters sometimes make. However, looking at the font table more closely I realized it's that tiny Underwood picture!

### Post by Piraja on 2009-02-06
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> openbox, conky, urxvt, cplay. the wallpaper is an andrew wyeth painting (yup, he died recently).
Usually I'm a bit sceptic about the idea of having "real"* art (such as oil paintings) reproduced as desktop backgrounds, but this is good, a way to commemorate. Tasty as always, Chucky.
___

* Before anyone flares me for this: I don't mean that e.g. electronic art isn't real, or art. Pay heed to the "ironic" function of the quotation marks. It's just that e.g. old-skool oil paintings, figurative or non-figurative, do not usually match very well with glossy icons, Emerald themes and other eye candy. See my avatar for a confession of a snobbish aesthete.

### Post by Islington on 2009-02-06
> **ArtF10 said:**
> You knew this question had to be coming:

How did you get 4 different wallpapers(1 for each workspace)?
 
Kde 4.X handles multiple desktops as multiple desktops. Gnome handles them as different workspaces. The next version of gnome (2.2x?) will have a patch to handle different wallpapers for different workspaces.


edit: attached screenshot/

### Post by billgoldberg on 2009-02-06
> **ArtF10 said:**
> You knew this question had to be coming:

How did you get 4 different wallpapers(1 for each workspace)?

Using the "wallpaper" plugin in Compiz Fusion.

In Gnome you first have to disable the drawing of the wallpaper by Nautilus in the gconf-editor.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-02-07
> **urukrama said:**
> I never heard of Andrew Wyeth before you posted your previous screenshot (should I be ashamed or embarassed?), but thanks for teaching me a little art. I quite like his paintings.

ashamed or embarassed? no, but he's pretty famous. like norman rockwell, he got a lot of crap from art critics as being an "illustrator". apparently, representational art was considered not artistic in the 20th century, unless of course you went overboard with it, like richard estes. (he may have dressed too normally, as well). to me, he seems like an artistic decendent from winslow homer, thomas cole and the like.

### Post by Mr. Picklesworth on 2009-02-07
This may make a few people cry:
[ATTACH]102587[/ATTACH]

Yes, minimalists, I have outminimalized all of you! (Okay, maybe not the Openbox people).

Yes, that is a vertical dual screen layout. Don't worry, it's a laptop; I have an excuse.

I decided to try out the Global Menu applet now that it is just an applet (using a nice GTK module for the dirty work instead of needing weird compile-time patching). I'm not actually convinced with the global menu bar idea, especially since the present hack makes it impossible to edit menu bars in Glade, but I rarely use menu bars anyway (I consider any interface which requires their use to be entirely broken). I decided it would be nice to get the things out of my way. Opens up some vertical space, confuses people and gives my top panel something to do so it doesn't go around terrorizing the neighbourhood.

I think it's quite attractive as a whole, and quite usable for me since I love my hotkeys. I wish Prelude (the Metacity theme I'm using) had just a LITTLE bit of a title bar :)

I have decided that I must use this theme continually. It is one of my goals to improve the window / task management experience, so what better incentive than to pick something which is absolutely unusable for most end users and come up with the lofty goal to "make this understandable, intuitive and easy for anyone?"
(Well, except the global menu part).

Here's another tip for the day! The new-fangled GDM-new (which is not yet stable), while rather weird with keyboards at times, seems to have cut my login time in half. You can see the little assistive technology applet it seems to stick me with on my notification area :)

---

### Post by Mr. Picklesworth on 2009-02-08
> **dbbolton said:**
> I think pretty much any desktop using gnome-panel is far from minimal. Aside from that, it looks like you're using 71.3% of your available memory and 52.9% of your swap (rough estimate).

In fairness, I'm running a very heavy virtual machine (another 32-bit Ubuntu), a web browser based on Gecko (consuming a solid 400 MB of RAM, probably partly thanks to Flash), a torrent and a bunch of development tools. Although yah, I was rather surprised by the performance there. Usually it never touches the swap, but it really didn't like something about that VM. After I installed Guest additions in there it worked better :)

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-02-09
A small update:

All of the following have been heavily modified:
GTK:  Murrine Clean Glass
Emerald:  Dots Emerald
Conky:  Mira
Dock: Cairo-Dock

The following have not been modified at all:
Font: Futura LT Condensed
Wallpaper: [Field for Escapists]("http://polar-is.deviantart.com/art/field-for-escapists-110509734")

Wallpaper: [Field for Escapists]("http://polar-is.deviantart.com/art/field-for-escapists-110509734")

Basically, the only thing I changed was the coloring and the wallpaper.  As you can see, I probably need to work on the coloring some more as the theme is more golden while the wallpaper is clearly coppery.

that wallpaper is great with those theme elements. matching conky's transparency to that of the icons (is that awn?) might be the only thing i'd do to it. 
as far as matching the 'golden' is concerned, i think the copper goes well with it. if everything starts to match, it can make everything look too flat.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-02-09
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> that wallpaper is great with those theme elements. matching conky's transparency to that of the icons (is that awn?) might be the only thing i'd do to it.

Yeah, I used devilspie to change the transparency of Conky and Compiz to change the transparency of Cairo-Dock.  I think Conky is set at 70% and Cairo-Dock is set at 56%.  I think I'll set them both at 65% as a compromise.

> as far as matching the 'golden' is concerned, i think the copper goes well with it. if everything starts to match, it can make everything look too flat.I think I understand you on that.  If I try to match the theme too closely to the wallpaper, nothing in my desktop would stand out anymore.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-02-09
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I think I understand you on that.  If I try to match the theme too closely to the wallpaper, nothing in my desktop would stand out anymore.

right. the same color, in different levels of light, will appear to be different shades. having the different shades gives the appearance of the three dimensional in a two dimensional medium (your desktop in this case), as some objects will appear to be a further distance from the source of light, or being lit by a different source that may be further away, or at a different angle.

### Post by Piraja on 2009-02-09
Since I mentioned Malevich's "Black Square" I had to try out how it could be put to use. Sacrilegous but astonishing: all I had to do in order to make that wallpaper was to left-click the image (of M:s painting as seen in the FF window) in Midnight Commander, right-click in the Feh window that opened and choose a "seamless" setting of the background in the menu dialog.

Loma is a pretty nice theme for this desktop, I think. And as you can see, even the "Black Square" is actually brown!

**P.S.** Oh yes &#8212; as you might figure out, looking at the virgin bookmark toolbar of Firefox, this is today's fresh install of Xubuntu 8.04 + Openbox on a spare partition on an oldish Compaq that keeps talking to me leisurely: I'm hearing "Scrunch scrunch" or something like that. The sofa-like upholstering with a true modern classic(!) suits so well this good old workhorse!

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-02-09
> **G@B0 said:**
> Of course, I'll love to add that widget to my desktop.

I've uploaded the widget to my google code account [here]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/amarokwidget.tar.bz2").  Inside the tarball is the skz file, a fonts folder with a font that you need for the theme, and a python script called amrk.py. The python script is a little help program that pulls information from amarok. It just needs to be somewhere in your path. On my box it's located at /usr/local/bin/amrk.py. I used to use qdbus to get info from amarok, but I've found that it seems to make dbus-daemon leak memory like crazy. The script also allows it to do things like disappear completely when amarok isn't running or is stopped. Let me know if you have any problems with it.

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-02-10
> **le singe said:**
> eightmillion, I've got to say that's one of the nicest KDE desktops I've seen, it's getting me considering giving KDE another shot...

Can you give the details? (wallpaper, icon theme, OS...)

Thanks. First, to the five people that downloaded the amarok widget, there was a couple mistakes with it. It wasn't showing the frame at all and the last.fm cover was totally wrong. I've uploaded the new version [here.]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/amarokwidget.tar.bz2") If you installed it through plasma, you can just put the new skz file in the folder ~/.kde/share/apps/plasma/plasmoids/sk_amarok-hipster/ and it will update it.

Now, about the theme, here are some details.

[Wallpaper]("http://manicho.deviantart.com/art/Monday-Wallpaper-50805568")
[Icons]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Refit+Black?content=89298")

The widget style is [bespin]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Bespin?content=63928") and the plasma theme is called [plateau]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Plateau?content=97720"). The colors and window decoration are custom. I've uploaded them [here]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/hip.tar.bz2"). That file includes a bespin config, the amarok widget, the color scheme, and some fonts. The window decorations require dekorator. Both dekorator and bespin should be in the Ubuntu repositories. I think that's about it. Let me know if you need anything else.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-02-11
> **cdwillis said:**
> What are you using to display those RSS feeds?

Conky +

```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Lucida Grande:size=6.3
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color ffffff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 252525
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 afafaf #bfbfbf #cfcfcf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 111111 #1a1a1a #720000
color4 0a0a0a #101010

own_window yes
own_window_colour 0a0a0a
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
```

### Post by kk0sse54 on 2009-02-11
> **Sorivenul said:**
> So, how is Gentoo these days? That screenshot makes me want to try it again, but its up-and-down development over the past year or two has me rather put off.

I love Gentoo, but there's definitely been an increase focus on stability whereas it used to be the new and kinda of "bleeding edge" distro sort of what Arch is regarded these days as. I mean just to get my set up I had to run a ~x86 system and unmask KDE 4.2 (or there was also the possibility of installing an overlay). I know there's been a lot of developer in fighting and what some perceive to be a lack of focus but for the most part I can't give much of a valid opinion on that since I've only been using Gentoo for little bit less than about 3 months. Otherwise from what I've seen development seems to be going along great especially in regards to Portage and the switch to weekly tarballs to provide a more update to date installation.

---

### Post by dmizer on 2009-02-12
> **voxman69 said:**
> Mark76 >> You're right. I did shrink my pics a little. In the first post in this thread it was stated that the pics that were uploaded to this server couldn't be higher than 800x600, and since mine are 1024x600 I thought it was best to shrink.

Sorry if it made the details hard to see.

Just for the record:

Maximum file size for an attached JPG is 19.5 KB. The 800x600 restriction is for hotlinked images only.

So this is unacceptable:
[noparse][img]www.some-site.com/some-giant-image.jpg[/img][/noparse]

But this is perfectly fine:
[noparse][[img]www.some-site.com/thumbnails/nice-tiny-thumbnail.jpg[/img]](www.some-site.com/some-giant-image.jpg)[/noparse]

### Post by jenkinbr on 2009-02-14
Here's my details (took forever to look them all up)



GTK: Divinorum-Revisited-1.2 ( [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Divinorum-Revisited?content=89200](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Divinorum-Revisited?content=89200) )

Icon: Ubuntu Simplicity 8.10 ( [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ubuntu+Simplicity+8.10?content=94592](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ubuntu+Simplicity+8.10?content=94592) )

Menu Icon: Circle Starts 0.9 ( [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Circle+Starts?content=95970](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Circle+Starts?content=95970) )
--Extracted Pack to ~/.icons/
--Modified Gconf value at /apps/panel/objects/object_0/custom_icon to point to the Ubuntu icon
--Modified Gconf value at /apps/panel/objects/object_0/use_custom_icon to 1
----NOTE: Your Menu object *may* be somethiing other than 'object_0', look for an object_type of 'menu-object'
----NOTE: I could not get this to work with the menu bar.

Font: Vibrocentric ( [http://www.dafont.com/vibrocentric.font](http://www.dafont.com/vibrocentric.font) )

Emerald: Modified from Emerald-Ubuntu-edit ( [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Emerald+Ubuntu+edit?content=76413](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Emerald+Ubuntu+edit?content=76413) )

wallpaper: Ubuntu Space Ring ( [http://setasbackground.blogspot.com/2008/11/ubuntu-space-ring.html](http://setasbackground.blogspot.com/2008/11/ubuntu-space-ring.html) )
--I made some color and level adjustments in GIMP

Skydome: Constructed from a nexuiz pacage out of skybox images.
--Nexuiz package is cttourney1_nex.pk3. ( [http://maps.nexuizninjaz.com/cttourney1_nex.pk3](http://maps.nexuizninjaz.com/cttourney1_nex.pk3) )
--You only need the /env/stratosphere/ directory from the .pk3 archive.
--I used a GIMP plugin called pandora to put it together.  It is in the pandora package (universe).

CubeCaps (err, spherecaps?): ubuntu-logo-transparentcubecap-1440x900, found at (  )

That's gnome-terminal on the desktop running htop (in universe repo).  I accomplished this using an app called 'devilspie' (also in universe repo). A tutorial can be found on page 10 of Full Circle Magazine Issue 7. ( [http://fullcirclemagazine.org/issue-7/](http://fullcirclemagazine.org/issue-7/) )

Other apps:
--foobillard (universe)
--leafpad (universe)

### Post by Islington on 2009-02-15
> **BDNiner said:**
> I am a big fan of Glassy Bleu. Only problem is that OOo looks horrible. It defaults to the high contrast icons and make it unbearable to look at.

cant you just use another theme?

just write a shell script if you are lazy like me

```
#!/bin/bash
# This changes the appearance of idiotic applications
# Your favorite theme = GTKRCFILE
# GTK2_RC_FILES = path to your favorite theme's gtkrc (change /usr/share/themes to /home/*whatever*.themes if you wish)
GTKRCFILE=Human
GTK2_RC_FILES=/usr/share/themes/"$GTKRCFILE"/gtk-2.0/gtkrc "$@"

```

save it as *whatever* 
make it executable (chmod or use gui)
test it by running 
```
cd /(wherever you have the shell script saved)  *whatever* ooffice -writer 
```
change the menus using the menu editor.

edit: check it out: I am running cianosmooth with ooffice-writer.

---

### Post by RiceMonster on 2009-02-16
> **ghindo said:**
> how I wish foobar were a) Open source b) For Linux :(

Don't really care about a but b is a biggy. Nothing on Linux is nearly as good.

> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> in runs pretty well in wine.

It was all crashy when I tried it. Like it would lock up when I opened the equalizer. Plus, is it possible to make it work with last.fm if you're running it in wine?

> **-jay- said:**
> how do u post a screenshot ?

You can upload one as an attachment, or you can use an image hosting site like [http://www.xs.to](http://www.xs.to). If you want to take a screenshot, I'm pretty sure you can do it in default Ubuntu simply by pressing print screen. If not,

```
sudo apt-get install scrot
```

then

```
scrot -cd3
```

And you'll get a screenshot in 3 seconds.

### Post by Piraja on 2009-02-17
> **-jay- said:**
> heres mine

[[IMG]http://img209.imageshack.us/img209/3126/screenshottc1.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img209.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshottc1.jpg)
Very nice! Except for Imageshuck's pop-up poker advertisement. You asked how to post a screenshot; I would say the best way is to use Ubuntu Forums' attachment feature (scroll down when you are writing a new post and look for "Attach a file / Manage attachments"; when editing an earlier post, you must enable "Advanced options" to replace the attachment or to add a new one). For taking a screenshot in Ubuntu, GNOME Screenshot Tool comes in very handy. I often use it also on Openbox, even though it lacks some features there. In any case, I don't really see the advantages of scrot if you're using GNOME. And "prt scr" does not allow for delay.

---

### Post by jenkinbr on 2009-02-17
> **Islington said:**
> cant you just use another theme?

just write a shell script if you are lazy like me

```
#!/bin/bash
# This changes the appearance of idiotic applications
# Your favorite theme = GTKRCFILE
# GTK2_RC_FILES = path to your favorite theme's gtkrc (change /usr/share/themes to /home/*whatever*.themes if you wish)
GTKRCFILE=Human
GTK2_RC_FILES=/usr/share/themes/"$GTKRCFILE"/gtk-2.0/gtkrc "$@"

```

save it as *whatever* 
make it executable (chmod or use gui)
test it by running 
```
cd /(wherever you have the shell script saved)  *whatever* ooffice -writer 
```
change the menus using the menu editor.

edit: check it out: I am running cianosmooth with ooffice-writer.

Thanks, always wondered how I could do that.

> **raul_ said:**
> Why have I been stripped off 30 beans in the past 2 days? :KS

The admins stripped the archives a bit, that's probably where your thirty beans went.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-02-19
> **juanmoreno92 said:**
> Can you spot the diff(erence)? Is it XP or GNOME?
[http://i192.photobucket.com/albums/z256/uncholowapo/thediff.png](http://i192.photobucket.com/albums/z256/uncholowapo/thediff.png)

1.  The close, minimize, and maximize buttons should be about one or two pixels lower.
2.  There is no shadow on the titlebar text on the real Royale theme.
3.  The notification area has a lighter color on the real Royale theme.
4.  The scrollbars have three lines in the middle of them.

Other than these four (minor) details, I'd say this theme looks almost exactly like XP's new Royale theme.

Would you mind sharing it?  I like the look of the taskbar (specifically the window list buttons) and I want to tinker with it for a theme I'm working on.

### Post by BazookaAce on 2009-02-19
Okay, i'm working on my new desktop, and i'm having a problem with my conkysetup. As you can see on the screenshot, i want to move my conky a little bit up. How can i do that? I'm new to conky, so... My screen is 1024x600, so it's to small to fit the whole thing like it is now. 

[[IMG]http://img25.imageshack.us/img25/6032/screenshot18mf4.th.png[/IMG]](http://img25.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot18mf4.png)

Here's my conky setup:

[HTML]background no
double_buffer yes
use_xft yes

default_color gray
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
own_window_transparent yes



#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys

own_window  yes

own_window_transparent no

own_window_type normal

own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 



#borders

draw_borders no

border_margin 0



#shades

draw_shades no



#position

gap_x 0

gap_y -5

alignment top



#behaviour

update_interval 1



#colour

default_color  gray



#default_shade_color 000000

own_window_colour 000000



#font

use_xft yes

xftfont bauhaus:pixelsize=9



#to prevent window from moving

use_spacer no

minimum_size 1024 0
maximum_size 1024




TEXT

  ${color white}${time %I:%M %p}$color ${time %A, %b %d %Y}  |  ${exec whoami} @ ${nodename}  |  ${color} Up: ${color white}${uptime_short}   |  ${color}Cpu: ${color white}${cpu}%  ${color}${cpugraph 10,85 AEA08E 9F907D} ${color white}  |  ${color }Mem: ${color white}$mem/$memmax - $memperc% ${membar 6,85}${color }  |  Home: ${color white}${fs_used /home}  / ${fs_size /home}  - ${fs_used_perc /home}% ${fs_bar 6,85} | ${color}Temp: ${color white}${acpitemp}C
  ${color}Network: ${color white}${wireless_essid eth1} ${wireless_link_qual_perc eth1}  |  ${color}Net: ${color white}${font}${downspeed eth1} Kb/s ${color}  ${downspeedgraph eth1 10,85 AEA08E 9F907D}  ${color white} ${totaldown eth1} down  |  ${color}Email: ${color white}${execi 300 python ~/scripts/gmail.py} | ${execi 3600 perl ~/scripts/weather.pl USVA0652 f t} ${execi 3600 perl ~/scripts/weather.pl USPA1290 f c}  |  ${color}Battery: ${color white}${battery_percent}% ${battery_bar 6,85}  |  ${color} Now playing: ${color white}${exec audtool --current-song}  ${exec audtool --current-song-output-length}/${exec audtool --current-song-length-[/HTML]

---

### Post by m_duck on 2009-02-19
> **BazookaAce said:**
> ii want to move my conky a little bit up. How can i do that?

Get rid of the blank line underneath TEXT. That should move it up a bit. If it needs to go up further, change the "gap y" to something like "-10" and see. Having said that, you might want to change "gap y" to 0 after removing that line.

It's just completely transparent, and it still includes that white line. As far as the karamboid goes, [here it is.]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/scotch.tar.bz2") Same instructions apply as last time. There are some fonts included, and the amrk.py python script needs to be somewhere in your path.

Edit: Thanks crimesaucer. :)  I just saw your post.

karamboid...Why didn't they come up with that?

I'm sorry but what instructions where those? I must have missed them :(

### Post by raul_ on 2009-02-19
Never mind, I've found them :)

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-02-19
> **raul_ said:**
> karamboid...Why didn't they come up with that?

I'm sorry but what instructions where those? I must have missed them :(

Karamboid just sounds right, but it appears that I may be the only one calling them that. :( The instructions are basically what I listed in the previous post. The theme uses Segoe for the font, which is included in the archive. There's also a python script in the archive that needs to go in one of these folders: /usr/local/sbin:/usr/local/bin:/usr/sbin:/usr/bin:/sbin:/bin:/usr/games. Then it's just a matter of loading the skz file.

---

### Post by raul_ on 2009-02-19
What about that? Naked without lines ;) Just go to System Settings -> Desktop Theme Details, edit anything you like and then select "Customized" from the Plasma themes list. I replaced the "Task Items" theme for the Glaze one.

I'm still trying to get the karamboid working. It's there (I can click it) but it's invisible.

EDIT: I don't know if it helps, but manually running the script it spits out '0'. I've looked in the code but cann't find out why it exits :(

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-02-19
> **raul_ said:**
> Yeap, I've made sure of that. Maybe it's not detecting it for some reason. Do you have any other dependencies?

You run Arch, right? You might check to see if python-dbus is installed and also, pgrep. I'm not sure what the shell is that superkaramba invokes either, but that theme contains many bashisms. I would say the most likely cause is that the theme just isn't finding that script. You might try running it from the command line with "superkaramba scotch.skz". See if it spits out any useful debugging info.

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-02-20
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> how did you get the menu icon to be the gnome icon and not the xfce mouse one?
I think with xfce4-menu-plugin, the easiest way is to just Right click on it > Properties > Button icon. You can put a path to an image file or an icon name like "start-here".

### Post by baizon on 2009-02-21
> **crimesaucer said:**
> This is difficult to do since I customize everything myself:


- I use the murrine-svn engine and write my own gtkrc themes.
- I also make my own Emerald theme. This one uses the close buttons of a theme called "Radial")
- Icons are both the hydroxygene icon pack and the MacUltimate Leporard buttons. (I replace the gtk-buttons in the hydroxygene with the Apple ones for my browser/file manager)
- Some icons are from the iComity for my xfce4-panel launchers.
- The xfce4-panel is using a cairo patch for RGBA transparency.
- Font is called LucidaMACBold.
- Screenlets have all been modified to use different .png and .svg images and I also edit the python scripts to use my LucidaMACBold font and change the pager's colors.
- Slim theme is also the same as my wallpaper to seamlessly go from login to desktop.
- I also use a gtkrc-2.0 for my xfce4-panel for button/font colors.
- And the conkyrc is my own custom script that I made.


..... I might upload some of my murrine-svn gtk themes one of these days.

Thats his details :)

---

### Post by wipeout140 on 2009-02-21
> **myusername said:**
> they aren't Eikon.
Gaia Nova GTK Theme, Axe Xfce theme, Simple Icons

Few of the icons are from Eikon like the start here and openoffice icons and he is credited in the authors file along with rest of people who icons i used in theme pack. 

Simple was designed for the computers i created through second hand parts and gave way to people who could not afford brand new computers with Windows and Microsoft office etc... so installed Xbuntu or Ubuntu depending on the specs of the PC. The main goal was to give Linux a good modern image as most had not heard of Linux so made sure it looked good and performed well from the first boot for them

Am glad people are using and enjoying the theme pack

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6739605&postcount=605](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6739605&postcount=605)

For the complete "Simple" Look

[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Simple?content=99470&PHPSESSID=fcc9797a3de35f0ebbe0ed661860413a](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Simple?content=99470&PHPSESSID=fcc9797a3de35f0ebbe0ed661860413a)

Link to gnome look  - Simple Download

### Post by crimesaucer on 2009-02-21
Thank you to everyone.

@ Giant Speck - I did sort of go for a mac look, but still with a solid Linux look using murrine/emerald and no dock. The Mac buttons are what really pull this theme together (and the transparency). I wish someone would make some Linux "back/forward" metal-buttons that were similar to the Mac ones..... but even better.


@ zekopeko - baizon pretty much summed it up. I stick with a constant theme that I make variations of. This one I changed the xfce4-panel patch to use the RGBA colors of "0, 0, 0, 0.8" to make it black and less transparent. Then I matched my emerald, screenlets, and terminal to all be #000000 and 80% opacity. The theme is based on a murrine theme that I made a couple of months ago..... I just fixed the gradient to look a bit better and I added a few other modifications to have a silver/chrome look to it. (I also edited all of my screenlet .svg images to not have the glossy effects.... so that they matched the emerald/conky/xfce4-panel look..... and I messed around with the pager image to make it look better.)


And I recently added the weather script to my .conkyrc from here: [http://sen7.deviantart.com/art/Conky-Mira-100078939](http://sen7.deviantart.com/art/Conky-Mira-100078939)


then I added a solid black #000000 background (like the deviantART conkys) and made that transparent with compiz-fusion's "opacity" plugin.



I have been trying to perfect these theme so I can finally release some versions/variations of it. When I finally upload something I will post all of the links for everybody.

---

### Post by linuxisevolution on 2009-02-21
> **dbbolton said:**
> Pretty zippy, that's for sure.

How different is fvwm-crystal from regular fvwm? I've been playing around with it lately.

I don't know since I never tried fvwm. Is fvwm the windows95-like window manager, or is that qvwm? So many WM's... Fvwm-crystal is very nice and is organized and fast- along with transparency the ability to customize -if you know pearl:D. Fvwm also integrates the customization of menus, backgrounds, and window boarders all into the crystal menu. I don't mean to sound like an add, I just really like it lol.:p

EDIT: I just realized I wrote a whole page on my website about wm's.[http://98.219.177.90/apache2-default/thelinuxhowto/lwm.html](http://98.219.177.90/apache2-default/thelinuxhowto/lwm.html)

### Post by ddnev45 on 2009-02-21
> **dbbolton said:**
> Pretty zippy, that's for sure.

How different is fvwm-crystal from regular fvwm? I've been playing around with it lately.

Fvwm-crystal is an elaborate fvwm theme and configuration with associated scripts. More resource hungry than fvwm, oviously, but not as resource intensive as gnome.

Minor tweaks to my fvwm setup; pretty much have the look I want.

typical misconceptions from an outsider. here's how it goes, amateur:

1 - do a google image search for a pic related to one's current, fleeting fancy
2 - expand image to 1280x800, no matter how inappropriate
3 - use the same stupid icons and fonts you always use
4 - you were correct on this one
5 - or dwm (unless going through some weird gnome/kde/xfce4 period of doubtfulness)
6 - show it off instantly (as the world will want to know)
7 - change it immediately, using the same process

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-02-23
Prepping for the release of Macchiato 0.2:

[LIST]
[*]I have finally fixed the bug where if you selected something and then unfocused the window, it would change the color of the selected item to where it would appear to be gray text on a gray background.
[*]I changed the color of the notebook header so that it matched the buttons.
[*]I tweaked some text color configurations.
[*]And finally, I made some changes to the panel colors and configuration.
[/LIST]
Here are the details of the following screenshots:

[LIST]
[*]Wallpaper:  [Speck]("http://jaj43123.deviantart.com/art/Speck-113369610")
[*]GTK:  Macchiato 0.2
[*]Icons: Eikon
[*]Font: Gill Sans MT
[*]Panel background:  [Smoke]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Smoke+-+a+gnome+panel+bg?content=99748")
[/LIST]
To compensate for the large bottom panel, I have removed the top panel, conky, and cairo-dock.  I may try to develop a horizontal conky to place at the top and then have cairo-dock auto-hide at the top of the screen.

Macchiato 0.2 is almost ready for release and I should have it up later on today on GNOME-Look, so keep an eye out for it!

---

To compensate for the large bottom panel, I have removed the top panel, conky, and cairo-dock.  I may try to develop a horizontal conky to place at the top and then have cairo-dock auto-hide at the top of the screen.

Macchiato 0.2 is almost ready for release and I should have it up later on today on GNOME-Look, so keep an eye out for it!

Very smooth and coffee like. :)

---

### Post by Tux Aubrey on 2009-02-24
> **ddnev45 said:**
> Where did you get the Places gadget? I don't recall sing that one in my e17 -- also the OzOs script.

Places was added to the E-MODULES_EXTRAS package early this year (I think).  It is also available at [http://code.google.com/p/e17mods/wiki/Places](http://code.google.com/p/e17mods/wiki/Places)

The scripts I use are e17_svn.sh (as in [this thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=916690")) and update_e17.sh (part of the oz-e17-tools / oz-desktop suite described in this [How-To]("http://cafelinux.org/OzOs/content/how-install-ozos-desktop-existing-os")).  Both scripts are by Rui Pais but e17_svn.sh is based on [easy_e17.sh by Morlenxus]("http://exchange.enlightenment.org/application/show/134").

---

and it has another nice effect :) i can use the xfce desk menu even above the now playing screenlet at the top of my screen (size 1280x100), which was not possible before

### Post by tjwoosta on 2009-02-27
> **Lord DarkPat said:**
> Can you please give the theme details? It's a very nice setup. The gloss is executed very well.

sure

gtk theme is called overglossed
[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Overglossed?content=74813]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Overglossed?content=74813")

font is called snap, but i cant remember exactly where i found it sry 
(you can probably just search google and find it)


awesome theme
```

font          = snap 12

bg_normal     = #222222
# bg_focus      = #535d6c
bg_focus      = #1d78a6
bg_urgent     = #ff0000

fg_normal     = #aaaaaa
fg_focus      = #ffffff
fg_urgent     = #ffffff

border_width  = 1
border_normal = #222222
border_focus  = #535d6c
border_marked = #91231c

# There are another variables sets
# overriding the default one when
# defined, the sets are:
# [taglist|tasklist]_[bg|fg]_[focus|urgent]
# titlebar_[bg|fg]_[normal|focus]
# Example:
#taglist_bg_focus = #ff0000

# Display the taglist squares
taglist_squares_sel = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/taglist/squarefw.png
taglist_squares_unsel = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/taglist/squarew.png

tasklist_floating_icon = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/tasklist/floatingw.png

# Variables set for theming menu
# menu_[bg|fg]_[normal|focus]
# menu_[border_color|border_width]
menu_submenu_icon = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/submenu.png
menu_height   = 15
menu_width    = 100

# You can add as many variables as
# you wish and access them by using
# beautiful.variable in your rc.lua
#bg_widget    = #cc0000

# Define the image to load
titlebar_close_button_normal = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/titlebar/close.png
titlebar_close_button_focus = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/titlebar/closer.png

# You can use your own command to set your wallpaper
wallpaper_cmd = awsetbg /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/background.png

# You can use your own layout icons like this:
layout_dwindle = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/dwindlew.png
layout_fairh = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/fairhw.png
layout_fairv = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/fairvw.png
layout_floating = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/floatingw.png
layout_magnifier = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/magnifierw.png
layout_max = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/maxw.png
layout_spiral = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/spiralw.png
layout_tilebottom = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/tilebottomw.png
layout_tileleft = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/tileleftw.png
layout_tile = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/tilew.png
layout_tiletop = /usr/share/awesome/themes/default/layouts/tiletopw.png

awesome_icon = /usr/share/awesome/icons/awesome16.png


```

wallpaper called frozentree or something like that
[[img]http://omploader.org/tMWIyNw[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMWIyNw)

i think thats everything, if not just ask
